  193. # [01:10] <sicking> nsm: do we enforce CSP even when there's a service worker?
  194. # [01:11] <nsm> sicking: do you mean when there is a serviceworker intercepting a request?
  195. # [01:11] <sicking> nsm: right
  196. # [01:11] <sicking> nsm: so if I load a HTML page which uses CSP to say that scripts must be loaded from https://myscripts.mysite.com/, then is that guaranteed even if the page uses SW?
  197. # [01:12] <nsm> sicking: fetch() called form a SW does obey CSP. the problem is right now we don't pass the right csp context so all of it is treated as a 'fetch' csp type
  198. # [01:13] <sicking> nsm: not just that, but we need to track where each response was loaded from, so that when the response is used as a response for a script load, that we enforce that it came from the right place
  199. # [01:13] <sicking> nsm: even if the response was originally loaded using a plain fetch()
  200. # [01:13] * Quits: Mano (mano@moz-ulq2b0.red.bezeqint.net) (Connection closed)
